<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Wireless power transfer (WPT) applications range from powering batteryless wireless sensors 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, radioâfrequency (RF) identification (RFID) 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, and implantable devices 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>â
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, to the higher scale of space-based solar cells and wirelessly charged 
electric vehicles. It utilizes various frequency bands starting from low megahertz for low-power implants 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> to ultrahigh-frequency (UHF) RFID tags 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, including a 433-MHz industrial, scientific, and medical (ISM) band 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> that is used for license-free communication, underwater wireless-sensor 
networks 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, and automotive applications such as batteryless tire-pressure monitoring 
systems 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. Among this myriad of batteryless devices, the wireless power receiver is 
considered the linchpin for any given WPT system.</p><p>As shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>, the RF-to-dc power converter is the core of any wireless power 
receiver that supplies usable dc power out of the incoming RF power to the antenna. Recently, an RF-to-dc power 
converter has been used for recycling wasted RF power in hybrid duplexers and enhancing the power amplifier efficiency 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>. The RF-to-dc power converter performance is evaluated in terms of two main 
parameters: 1) sensitivity, which defines the minimum input RF power required to generate a specific dc output voltage, 
and 2) power-conversion efficiency (PCE), which is the ratio of the usable output dc power

<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-8" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-11" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">P_{i}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and can be expressed by

where the input power

<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-79" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-80"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-81"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-82" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-83"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-84"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-85" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">o</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">P_{o}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the dissipated power in rectifying devices 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-86" role="math" style="width: 2.105em; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">P_{\mathrm{diss}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the reverse leakage power 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-98" role="math" style="width: 1.805em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.63em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-99"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-100"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-101" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-102"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-103"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-104"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-105"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-106" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-107" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">v</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-108" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">P_{\mathrm{rvs}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, 
which is caused by the nonidealities in the reverse characteristic of the rectifying device.</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda1-2591263-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda1-2591263-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda1-2591263_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda1-2591263_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig>
<p>Block diagram of the wireless power receiver.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7555334/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p>Traditionally, acâdc power converters have been realized using diode-based architectures, such as the 
Greinacher cell, the Dickson multiplier 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>, or a full-wave bridge rectifier 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>. Diode-based rectifiers have simply been realized in CMOS technology 
using diode-connected transistors, such as the Dickson rectifier shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2(a)</a>. However, they suffer from poor sensitivity at low input power 
and from high dropout voltage that degrades their PCE at mid-high input power. Enhanced sensitivity can be achieved 
either by using Schottky diodes that require additional fabrication steps and, hence, are seldom offered in 
conventional CMOS processes or by using an integrated step-up transformer occupying a large area 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>. On the other hand, the differential fully cross-coupled (FX) rectifier 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2(b)</a>, is widely used in RFID applications, due to its improved 
sensitivity and high peak efficiency. However, this improvement is gained at the expense of the reverse characteristic 
of the rectifying devices because the rectifying cross-coupled transistor is still a bidirectional device, unlike 
diodes or diode-connected transistors. Hence, it conducts in a reverse direction once the instantaneous value of the RF 
signal 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-109" role="math" style="width: 1.805em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.63em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-110"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-111"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-112" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-113"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-114"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-115"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-116"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-117" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-118" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">F</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">V_{\mathrm{RF}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> becomes lower than the output dc voltage 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-119" role="math" style="width: 1.925em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.75em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-120"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-121"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-122" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-123"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-124"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-125"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-126"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-127" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">D</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">D</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">V_{\mathrm{DD}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in every RF cycle, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3(a)</a>. This periodic reverse leakage is exacerbated as the RF power 
level grows, degrading the rectifier conversion efficiency at high input power, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3(b)</a>. Consequently, the rectifier operates efficiently within a 
limited range of input power. To evaluate different rectifier architectures, a dynamic range is defined as the input 
power range at which the rectifier maintains a PCE higher than 80% of its peak efficiency 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a>.</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda2ab-2591263-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda2ab-2591263-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda2ab-2591263_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda2ab-2591263_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 2. </b><fig>
<p>Schematic of (a) the Dickson rectifier and (b) the conventional FX rectifier.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7555334/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda3ab-2591263-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda3ab-2591263-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda3ab-2591263_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda3ab-2591263_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 3. </b><fig>
<p>(a) Conventional FX rectifier efficiency versus RF power and (b) its alternating current, output dc voltage, and RF 
voltage.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7555334/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p>In 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a> and 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, a low-megahertz adaptive architecture reconfigures the rectifier stage as 
a diode-connected voltage doubler or as a half cross-coupled rectifier based on the input power level. However, it 
requires active diodes driven by fast comparators that are not power efficient at high RF frequencies, such as UHF 433 
MHz or higher. A multistage configuration is presented in 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a> and 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a> to enhance the efficiency of the cross-coupled rectifier by rewiring 
stages as a series or parallel multistage rectifier. Although this technique extends the efficiency of the 
cross-coupled rectifier over a wide range of input power, it requires multiple stages with high input capacitance and 
low input resistance, thus complicating the matching network design. In 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a>, an adaptive offset calibration technique is presented to compensate the 
threshold voltage 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-129" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-130"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-131"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-132" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-133"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-134"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-135"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-136"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-137" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-138" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">V_{\mathrm{th}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> 
in diode-based rectifiers to improve their sensitivity. However, it requires two more auxiliary multistage rectifiers 
to compensate the 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-139" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-140"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-141"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-143"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-144"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-145"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-146"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-147" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-148" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">V_{\mathrm{th}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> 
of the main rectifier, thus occupying a large area, adding more losses and degrading the PCE.</p><p>In this brief, we propose and experimentally validate a self-biased cross-coupled differential CMOS rectifier with 
enhanced efficiency over a wider input range than both diode-connected and cross-coupled rectifiers. This facilitates 
reliable and efficient RF-to-dc power conversion at varying RF power levels, and it adds more spatial freedom between 
the wireless power transmitter and receiver. The proposed architecture is illustrated along with its operational 
concept in 
<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ II</a>, whereas the experimental results are discussed and compared 
with measurements of a fabricated conventional FX rectifier in 
<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III</a>. Finally, the conclusion is drawn in 
<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ IV</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Proposed RF-to-DC Power Converter</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Proposed Architecture</h3><p>A schematic of the proposed self-biased cross-coupled rectifier is shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>. The rectifier utilizes the cross-coupled configuration with the 
differential-drive capability, to maintain good sensitivity at low input power, by operating in the linear region and 
holding low dropout voltage. Moreover, a self-biasing mechanism is added to limit the reverse leakage at the sense of 
high input power. The proposed self-biasing mechanism controls the conduction of the rectifying devices by raising 
their effective turn-on voltage at high RF power levels. A simple implementation of this mechanism is achieved by 
applying the output dc voltage directly to the controlling gates of the rectifying transistors (MP1,2) without 
disturbing the RF signal at the differential inputs. This is achieved by decoupling the dc voltage of the rectifying 
pMOS MP1,2 gates from their corresponding nMOS MN1,2 using (CP3,4) and then applying the dc self-bias using an RF choke 
(RFC) coil that is a dc short circuit and an ac open circuit. It is worth noting that the self-biasing branch is 
connected to a MOSFET gate; hence, no dc current passes through it, whereas the self-biasing RFC branches can be simply 
replaced by high feedback resistors (RFB1, 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-149" role="math" style="width: 7.751em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.97em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.91em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-150"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-151" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">RFB</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-152" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-153" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-154" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">100</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-155" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-156" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-157" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">\text{RFB}2 \simeq 100\ \text{k}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) 
without loading the RF inputs, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>.</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda4-2591263-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda4-2591263-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda4-2591263_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda4-2591263_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 4. </b><fig>
<p>Schematic of the proposed self-biased cross-coupled rectifier.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7555334/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. Operational Concept</h3><p>The operating point of the proposed self-biased cross-coupled rectifying device is compared with the conventional 
cross-coupled and diode-connected rectifying devices in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>. Each rectifying device connects the ac-coupled 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-158" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.32em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-159"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-160" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">RF</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">\text{RF}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> node (RF superimposed on a common mode 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-161" role="math" style="width: 6.61em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.949em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.89em 2.646em -999.997em); width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-291"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-292"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-293" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-294" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">V_{\mathrm{DD}}/2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. 
This is unlike the conventional cross-coupled device, which requires 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-295" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-296"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-297"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-298" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-299"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-300"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-301"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-302"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-303" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-304" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">V_{\mathrm{th}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> 
only. Moreover, the proposed device conducts in the linear region and holds a dropout voltage of less than or equal to 
its overdrive voltage 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-305" role="math" style="width: 1.685em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.5em 2.526em -999.997em); height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-309"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-310"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-311"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-312"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-313" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-314" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-315" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">V_{\mathrm{eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, 
passing higher output voltage than the diode-connected device, which requires a dropout of 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-316" role="math" style="width: 4.568em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-317"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-318"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-319" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-320"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-321"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-322"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-323"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-324" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-325" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-326" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-327" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-328" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">V_{\mathrm{th}} + V_{\mathrm{eff}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. 
As a result, the proposed self-biased cross-coupled device retains moderate sensitivity (i.e., it generates higher 
output voltage at the same RF input power) compared with the diode-connected device. This is derived from the operating 
points shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> and it matches the simulated dropout voltages of the three 
rectifiers at the same input power, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(a)</a>.</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda5abc-2591263-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda5abc-2591263-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda5abc-2591263_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda5abc-2591263_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 5. </b><fig>

the conventional cross-coupled device is strongly biased by 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-360" role="math" style="width: 12.916em; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-393" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-395"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-396"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-397"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-398"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-399" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">D</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-400" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">D</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-401"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-402"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-403" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-404" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.463em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.403em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">V_{\mathrm{SG}({\mathrm{RVS}})} = V_{\mathrm{RF}}/2 + V_{\mathrm{DD}}/2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> 
in the reverse direction, as derived in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>. Accordingly, the reverse current lobes increase, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(b)</a>. On the other hand, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>, the proposed device is biased only at 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-405" role="math" style="width: 8.471em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 7.631em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1007.57em 2.766em -999.997em); width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-433"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-434"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-435" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-436" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; leading to reduced reverse current lobes, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(b)</a>. It is worth noting that, during the negative RF half-cycle, 
the gate of the MP1 in the conventional FX and proposed rectifiers is positively biased, shutting down its current 
completely, similar to the reverse-biased diode-connected device.</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda8ab-2591263-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda8ab-2591263-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda8ab-2591263_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda8ab-2591263_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 8. </b><fig>

resistors are highlighted.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7555334/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda9-2591263-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda9-2591263-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda9-2591263_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda9-2591263_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 9. </b><fig>

<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7(a)</a> shows the simulation of the output voltage versus the input 
power, for all three rectifiers, for a load of 50 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-437" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.2em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-438"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-439" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-440" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">\text{k}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. 
At low RF power, the proposed rectifier outperforms the Dickson rectifier, whereas it outperforms the FX rectifier at 
high RF power. This can be explained by plotting both the forward harvested charges and the reverse leakage charges at 
three distinct RF power levels, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7(b)</a>. The simulated PCE of the three rectifiers versus input power 
is plotted in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7(c)</a>. As shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>, the conventional FX rectifier has a peak PCE at low RF power, but 
it falls off rapidly due to its high reverse leakage current, which is shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(b)</a>. On the other hand, the Dickson (diode-based) rectifier 
displays a moderate PCE at the high RF power levels but suffers from poor efficiency at low input power due to its high 
dropout voltage, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(a)</a>. Conversely, the proposed rectifier achieves a wider dynamic 
range with a slight decrease in its peak PCE relative to the conventional FX rectifier.</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda10ab-2591263-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda10ab-2591263-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda10ab-2591263_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda10ab-2591263_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 10. </b><fig>

loads. (b) Measured dynamic range of the proposed and conventional rectifiers.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7555334/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda11-2591263-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda11-2591263-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda11-2591263_print-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/8920/7914797/7555334/ouda11-2591263_print-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 11. </b><fig>

various loads.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7555334/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p>A comparison of the three rectifying devices is summarized in 
<a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a>, where the proposed self-biased rectifying device shows 
competitive advantages of low dropout voltage, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(a)</a>, and hence low dissipation loss and better sensitivity than the 
diode-connected device. At the same time, the proposed rectifying device shows lower reverse leakage and wider input 
range than the conventional cross-coupled device, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 6(b)</a> and 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">7(c)</a>, respectively.</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TABLEâII </b>

<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Results and Discussion</h2></div><p>The proposed rectifier is implemented in a 0.18-
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-441" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-442"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-443" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-444" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">\mu\text{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> CMOS process technology and occupies a 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-445" role="math" style="width: 8.471em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 7.631em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1007.63em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-446"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-447" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">130</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-448" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-449" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-450" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-451" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-452" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">130</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-453" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-454" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-455" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">130\ \mu\text{m} \times 130\ \mu\text{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> 
active area. The die microphotograph is shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a>. A conventional FX rectifier is implemented on the same die for a 
fair comparison with the proposed rectifier, using identical test setup and conditions. The RF measurement setup 
includes an Agilent vector network analyzer (N5225A) and a digital multimeter (34420A). The rectifier's PCE is 
measured with a single-tone 433-MHz signal at different input power levels, and the output dc voltage is recorded. 
After deembedding the reflection and transmission losses, the net input power is calculated and the PCE for the 
proposed and conventional rectifiers is plotted in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a> versus the input power at different loads. Although the proposed 
rectifier has lower peak PCE (â65%) than the conventional rectifier, whose peak PCE is 
â75%, the proposed architecture maintains its PCE over a broader dynamic range of input power. Thus, the 
proposed rectifier can operate efficiently at different RF power levels, enabling robust wireless powering from varying 
transmission distances or within unstable environments.</p><p>To elucidate the relative PCE enhancement of the proposed rectifier, the ratio of the proposed rectifier PCE over 
the conventional FX rectifier PCE is plotted in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10(a)</a>, for variable loads 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-456" role="math" style="width: 4.147em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.727em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.67em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-457"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-458"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-459" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-460"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-461"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-462" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-463" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-464" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">50</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">R_{L} = 50</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, 100, and 200 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-465" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.2em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-466"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-467" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">k</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-468" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">\text{k}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. 
An approximately 40%â70% efficiency improvement is achieved in the proposed rectifier at mid-high 
input power 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-469" role="math" style="width: 5.288em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.748em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.63em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-470"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-471" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-472" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">&gt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-473" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">30</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-474" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-475" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-476" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">W</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-477" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">(&gt; 30\ \mu\text{W})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> 
relative to the conventional FX rectifier, as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10(a)</a>. Moreover, the proposed rectifier maintains the achieved 
improvement in PCE over a wide input range at different loading conditions, as shown in

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
